## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, where stress depends on strain through constitutive laws and temperature modifies material stiffness and flow behavior through thermal softening or activation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal modulus variation)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic stress-strain, Ramberg-Osgood type)
- Hollomon equation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with temperature dependence)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic with higher-order terms)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening for pre-strained materials)
- Hyperbolic sine flow rule: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep model inverted)
- Neo-Hookean with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * (epsilon + c2 * epsilon**3) (hyperelastic with cubic correction and thermal dependence)
- Bilinear model: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) + c3 * epsilon * T (strain-temperature cross coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) on stress terms
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation saturation
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 indicates work hardening in metals (n is strain hardening exponent)
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon) separating elastic limit from hardening contribution
- Thermally activated deformation → sinh or exp(c/T) terms reflecting Boltzmann-type activation over energy barriers
- Strain-temperature separability → Product form f(epsilon)*g(T) when mechanisms are independent; cross terms when coupled
- Rubber/polymer elasticity → Odd polynomial in strain (epsilon + c*epsilon**3) from entropic spring models
- Modulus linear in temperature → E = c0 + c1*T typical for metals well below melting point

`2.353524517872731*epsilon**2 + 6.266345790929248*epsilon*(T - 342.1714397168912)**2`

This contains a `T**2*epsilon` term, which is problematic for most candidates since they typically have at most linear T dependence or quadratic in epsilon.

This requires terms: `epsilon**2`, `epsilon*T**2`, `epsilon*T`, `epsilon`.

Most candidates have at most linear T. Let me look for candidates with `T**2` or `(T+...)**2` multiplied by epsilon-dependent terms.

**Candidate 90**: `T*c0 + T*c1*(c2 + epsilon)**2 + c3*epsilon + c4 + c5*epsilon*(T + c6)**c7`

- `T*c1*(c2+epsilon)**2 = T*c1*(c2**2 + 2*c2*epsilon + epsilon**2)`: need this to be 0, set c1=0
- `c3*epsilon + c4`: additional terms
- `c5*epsilon*T**2 + 2*c5*c6*epsilon*T + c5*c6**2*epsilon`

With c0=0, c1=0: `c3*epsilon + c4 + c5*epsilon*(T+c6)**2`

= `c4 + c3*epsilon + c5*epsilon*T**2 + 2*c5*c6*epsilon*T + c5*c6**2*epsilon`

But we need `epsilon**2` term and no constant term. We have no `epsilon**2` term available (c1=0 killed it). So this doesn't work with c1=0.

Let me keep c1 nonzero: `T*c1*(c2+epsilon)**2 = T*c1*c2**2 + 2*T*c1*c2*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2`

GT needs: no pure T term, no T*epsilon**2, but needs epsilon*T**2. So c1=0 (to kill T*epsilon**2), but then no epsilon**2.

**Candidate 144**: `c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon*(T + c4)**c5`
